Free Talk

Power and Majesty 151

— Jingwen

Reading the news from the Paris Conference these past few days in the newspaper is truly interesting. Many people are worried that a third world war may break out as a result, but I, like the slippery view of people like Tingli Ross, believe that although war is very "possible," it is also "not necessarily" so. Seeing British Foreign Secretary Bevin's sharp speech and Vyshinsky's retort certainly makes one sweat for the matter of war; however, seeing the photograph of American representative Austin and Vyshinsky laughing shoulder-to-shoulder, you almost suspect that they are at a cocktail party in the Palais de Chaillot.

International diplomacy is, of course, sacred and extraordinary. A single misstep can often lead to unexpectedly serious consequences, especially in the case of this United Nations General Assembly. The attending representatives are mostly heads of state from various countries, and their sighs and laughs become major headlines in the world's telecommunications. The situation of war and peace may be determined by a raise of their hands or a slam of their tables. It is not only sacred, but also extraordinarily important.

However, although the identity of international conference representatives is very important, they are still human beings of flesh and blood. They have emotions, common sense, and even humor. This column has previously published special features on the representatives of various countries at the conference, such as representatives who like to sketch portraits at the conference, representatives who love to write poetry, and representatives who are good at drawing curves. If you look past their representative identities, they are no different from a group of elementary school students in a classroom.

If we were to say that the fate of our world is decided by this group of people, it seems too incredible. Yet the fact cannot deny this point. Writing this, I can't help but think of Napoleon, as described by Tolstoy in his book "War and Peace." Napoleon's private life was very romantic. He even had to spray perfume before going into battle. That such a figure could lead an army, conquer Germany, Austria, England, and Russia, and become emperor is also a historical miracle. However, after the Battle of Waterloo, where was the hero of a generation? Napoleon was nothing more than an ordinary prisoner of war.

Whether a person is important or not has nothing to do with the person themselves, especially for politicians. The reason why politicians appear important is simply the power granted to them by their position. Once a person has a position and power, even if they still want to try to maintain their original human face, it is often impossible. Friends often say when they meet that so-and-so is now in power. The close relationship of munching spiced beans and peanuts together in the past can no longer be restored. Now, not only must one submit a name card before seeing them, but one can only nod and agree when meeting. So everyone says that so-and-so has become "snobbish" after gaining power. However, I can understand this kind of person very well. The person is still so-and-so at heart, but their position and power have to create a barrier between you, me, and them. Without sufficient courage, this barrier is not easily broken. Once they lose their position and power, they will still be able to return to the comradeship of spiced beans and peanuts.

What makes power and position a burden that individuals cannot get rid of is what is called majesty. The origin of majesty actually arises from people's illusions about the external appearances of things. For example, a dance hall will never give rise to a sense of majesty, but if it is changed into a solemn meeting hall, people who are in it cannot help but feel a sense of gravity, and a sense of majesty will also arise spontaneously. The Palais de Chaillot, where the Paris Conference is now located, was originally a museum. It has solemnity, but perhaps not true majesty. However, once it is converted into an international conference hall, and with all the people coming in and out being people with the highest power and status in the contemporary world, how can it not appear majestic?

Since majesty easily creates a heavy mood, and with everyone involved having their own power and status background, it is truly difficult to seek lighthearted peace negotiations in such an environment. The psychological reserve has long become an obstacle to harmony and cooperation. If verbal conflicts are encountered occasionally, it is rare for them not to become stalemates. We Chinese have always paid attention to the diplomacy of negotiating between cups of wine. The Western cocktail party is similar to this. If major international conferences in the future can be carried out in the sounds of "cheers, cheers," and if power, status, and the majesty that comes with them are seen as less important, then world peace may be hopeful.

Diluting the concept of power, status, and majesty is difficult for those involved, but easy for onlookers, because those involved are on the stage. The concept of "maintaining one's stage presence" is extremely difficult to break. Conversely, if the audience offstage can view the "plot" more plainly, without having to clap and cheer or boo, then the people onstage can easily come down, and they will not have to pretend and do a real show, or use real knives and guns. Our world now seems like a dance hall. The play is being acted, but it is still a fake play. We only ask that all parties in the audience can relax a step, and then the situation of real knives and guns can be avoided.

— Shi Shufan

Who is warming the old dream of Liang?

The autumn willows of the Taicheng are no more,

I only pity the imperial son's flowing literary talent,

Coming to the monk's tower to find traces.

Today, words and poems can no longer be mended,

Different dynasties have different views on the landscape.

The chickens turn ten thousand bamboos into divine arrows,

The setting sun silently sends the temple gate.

In the past, there were promises about life and death,

Now, no one discusses success or failure.

I ascended to a height, feeling a sense of vastness,

And even wrote a poem at the temple gate.

Patience, Resistance, Agility 156

— Yi Jun

My residence is in Zhabei, but my workplace is in Nanshi. Every morning I take the No. 2B public bus from Zhabei to Nanshi, and every afternoon I return from Nanshi to Zhabei. Speaking of taking the public bus, one needs several great skills, namely: patience, resistance, and agility.

As the name suggests, a public bus is not a private car for one person, so it cannot be available at any time. You must wait at the stop. While waiting, you must have patience. It is fortunate if the bus arrives in one or two minutes, and it is not bad luck if it arrives in five minutes or a quarter of an hour. But it is unlucky when you have to wait for half an hour, forty or fifty minutes. But you have to be patient - yelling, jumping, getting anxious, and cursing are useless.

You are not the only one waiting for the bus, and the more people wait, the more crowded it gets. So the arrival of the bus is a great joy, but getting on the bus is a major emergency. Before the bus stops, people have already surrounded the door in a circle. The people on the bus have not yet gotten off, but the people waiting to get on have already drawn their swords and are ready to charge into battle. Whoever is agile will get on first. At the same time, you have to have resistance. You have to be as stable as Mount Tai and as solid as a rock so that you are not pushed away by others. Your back and waist must be able to resist the pressure of other people's fists, arms, and kneecaps. Your feet must be prepared to be trampled on by others. You must seize any opportunity and enter any opening. See if you are that agile.

Is it all right once you get on the bus? No, you still have to be patient. If there is no seat, you have to stand. If people are pressing on you, hands are covering your head, or your head and neck are encircled, you can only be patient and only resist. Everyone is squeezed into a group, crushed into a pile. The pushing, bumping, and falling when the bus starts are needless to say. Sometimes, when the express bus stops suddenly, the whole bus of people falls sharply in the same direction. This "disaster" is unbearable. The production of carbon dioxide inside the bus is abundant, and the people who are coughing are not to be outdone, putting on a wonderful performance. There are also those who spit, showing great skill. With an open mouth, there is a whoosh, a mouthful of phlegm, like a meteor, like a missile, or like the white light of a swordsman, already crossing over your head and going outside the window. But when the phlegm passes over your head, there must be some scattered saliva, big beads and small beads falling on your head or sticking to your collar. You also have to be patient with this. Because there are many people of this kind, and if you interfere with them, they will not be honest, and will "retaliate with an eye for an eye and a tooth for a tooth." Since those who cough cough, and those who spit spit, naturally bacteria fly around, each seeking a host. Therefore, your body must have resistance, and then you can avoid contracting diseases.

The person sitting in front of you will not get off the bus, so there is no empty seat. You have to be patient. When there is an empty seat, you have to be agile so that you can grab the seat. If you fail to grab the seat, you still have to be patient.

This situation is not an exaggeration at all. I know that the trolleybus is better because it has a larger capacity. I take the public bus, the No. 2 public bus, and the No. 2 public bus with a "B" on it. There are surprisingly few buses, so this situation is never an exception. There is really never an exception. The situation is better with the No. 2 public bus without the "B", because there are more buses. The most commendable thing is the orderly queuing at the Qiujiang Road station, showing a clear order.

Because I take the No. 2B public bus every day, I have learned three major skills: patience, resistance, and agility.

Eastern Scales and Western Claws 157

— Jin Lin

The Arctic Tern can be called the traveler among birds. It is a type of seagull and flies between the North and South Poles every year, covering a total distance of almost 30,000 miles.

The Great Pyramid of Egypt has a total of more than 2.5 million yellow-gray stones, averaging three tons per block, transported from afar by tens of thousands of people, and the entire construction project took a total of twenty-five years.

The dreaded African poison, when produced, does not use eggs, but directly produces live pupae.

The Swiss eat the most milk in the world, with an average consumption of 526 pounds per person per year.

There are 3,064 languages in the world, but India alone has 179 languages and 480 dialects, making it the most linguistically complex country in the world.

Wang Huaizu's Hand-Annotated Yilin 158

— Qian Dacheng

Mr. Wang Huaizu (Niansun) of Gaoyou was a master of practical learning during the Qing dynasty. His book "Reading Miscellany" is already immortal. However, his hand-annotated classical books are rarely seen. In July of the thirty-fourth year of the Republic of China, I unexpectedly obtained his hand-annotated "Jiao Shi Yi Lin" at Songshi Studio in Suzhou. The original book was the "Jin Dai Mi Shu" edition from Jiguge. Initially, the bookseller did not mention whose annotations they were. I carefully examined it and found two large square seals, "Wang Family Collection of Gaoyou" and "Distinguished Family of Huaihai," confirming that it was once owned by Mr. Huaizu. The book is annotated in both red and black ink, meticulously referencing the Tang and Song dynasty encyclopedias "Youyang Zazu" and Mr. Lu Yidian of my county's Yilin school's collation of Song dynasty texts. The annotations are extensive, profound, and refined, unlike what one would expect from someone merely known as a book collector. The handwriting is extremely similar to that of Mr. Huaizu's annotated "Song Bao's Explanations of Characters, Supplemented with Lost Sections" in the Nanjing Longpanli National Academy of Learning Library. Comparing it with Wang's ink calligraphy in the "Chart of the Shuowen System," the resemblance is striking. Therefore, I know that it is Wang's hand-annotated edition without a doubt. I obtained it at a low price. Shouldn't I consider myself extremely fortunate? Throughout my life, I have been fortunate to see many old books, but due to my family's poverty, I could not keep them for myself, like clouds passing before my eyes. Only in the past did I obtain a fragment of Lu Baoyun's hand-annotated "Chuo Geng Lu" at a small price, which can be compared to this. I intend to transcribe some of his annotations to show them to those studying practical learning. The owner of Songshi Studio, Elder Zhang, passed away this spring. Recalling the joy of sitting and discussing art with him in the past is like another lifetime. I have also left Wumen (Suzhou) and returned to my hometown, and my interest in seeking books has greatly diminished. Fine books are also not often seen. I write this to record the shadows of past dreams.

Old News from the Double Tenth Festival, Newly Copied 159

— Song Xian

In the first year of the Republic of China, on the Double Tenth Festival, this newspaper's "Free Talk" section had a commemorative article that said: "What day is today? It is the first National Day of the Republic of China. Colorful flags are flying high, and the whole country is ecstatic. However, upon careful examination of national affairs, there are feelings in our hearts. Regarding domestic affairs, opinions are divided, and there is internal strife; regarding foreign affairs, the powers are watching like tigers, and recognition is uncertain; regarding finances, the Minister of Agriculture looks up at the roof, and resources are exhausted to meet needs; regarding military affairs, disbandment is not organized, and frequent alarms occur; the common people lack patriotism, and there are many rebellious elements in the border regions. The land is scarred, and it is unbearable to look back; the future is thorny, and how can we not be saddened! On this commemorative occasion, there are endless sighs, how can we force ourselves to follow the vulgar and engage in joyful celebrations?" Although times have changed, except for the "recognition" mentioned, it still seems to be applicable as a reflection on this year's Double Tenth Festival.

Also, in the first year of the Republic of China, on the Double Tenth Festival, the Founding Father attended the National Day celebration held by the Chinese Students' Association of the World in Shanghai. During his speech, he said: "...Although the Republic of China has been established, it is still in a dangerous era. Internal unrest has not been quelled, and foreign troubles are frequent. It is like building a tall building, the foundation has been laid, but it still needs to be constructed. I hope that my compatriots will have an adventurous spirit, a persevering spirit, and cooperate to support the government from now on to create a first-class power on earth. This is what I deeply hope for from you all..."

After copying the newspaper, I cannot help but sigh. I only hope that "future generations will view us as we view the past!"

###

Confucius said, "For three months, he did not know the taste of meat." If he were to patrol the streets and alleys of Beijing, especially during the autumn and winter months, he would smell the aroma of meat everywhere. The soil here is thick and lacks water, so the taste of fish and shrimp is far less fresh and delicious than in the south. However, the fatty and tender meat, especially mutton, and the cooking methods researched over hundreds of years are unparalleled in the country. The "Xikou mutton" from outside the Great Wall is considered the best. The three best ways to cook it are "stewing," "hot pot," and "roasting." "Stewing" refers to mutton of the highest quality, adding fragrant family secrets passed down for generations, hence the price is particularly high and business is flourishing. "Roasting" involves placing a large iron grate over a stove fire, cutting the meat into thin slices, mixing it with spices, sauce, and oil, allowing diners to use iron forks to skewer and roast the meat themselves, eating it as soon as it's cooked. It's exceptionally fresh and savory. A certain Wan family in the western part of the city is the most famous, but there is also one in the northern part of the city, and people flock to it in droves, having to queue for a spot as if at a bank run. And when eating, they spread their legs, extend their arms, and adopt postures like martial arts performers, opening their mouths like hungry tigers devouring food. It's both amusing and impressive. Even fashionable men and women gather in groups, roasting and devouring the meat with gusto, somewhat reminiscent of the "powder-faced girls, cutting raw meat to eat the pungent smell" in the Dream of the Red Chamber. "Hot pot" involves using a hot pot with burning charcoal in the center, the fire is fierce and the soup is boiling. Thin slices of mutton are prepared in advance, cooked briefly in the boiling soup, then taken out and dipped into a small bowl of sauce, wine, and various spices, mixed and eaten. It's rich, flavorful, and fatty, loved by many. In all of the above, the meat and hot pots are deliberately displayed outside the door, creating a lively and steaming scene as a form of advertisement. The ancient saying "wine ponds and meat forests" can be experienced in the old capital during the autumn and winter seasons.

Beef and mutton are difficult to popularize in the Beijing market, while pork remains the mainstream meat. The word "meat" is both a general term for all meat and a specific term for pork. If one refers to beef or mutton, one must specify beef or mutton. If one simply mentions "meat," everyone knows it means pork. Chicken and duck are also meat, but they are not referred to as "meat." In restaurants, chicken shreds and duck slices do not need to be specified as chicken meat shreds and duck meat slices, which is the opposite of pork, which is only referred to as "meat," also somewhat amusing. Currently, pork cannot be obtained in the Beijing market except on the black market. Beef, mutton, goose, and duck can still be obtained in the market, but fresh beef and mutton are not abundant, and although chicken and duck are plentiful, the prices are strangely high, and the quality is old, thin, and poor, each costing five or six yuan in gold coins. The so-called price limits are ignored by merchants, and no one questions them.

A poet said: "One can eat without meat, but one cannot live without bamboo." "Meat" is used to highlight "bamboo," and dwelling is considered essential with "bamboo." This shows that "meat" is also an essential part of food. The Four Books state, "When Confucius heard the Shao music in Qi, he did not know the taste of meat for three months," using "meat" to praise the Shao music, and thus the status of "meat" is not low. Those who satirize officials say, "Those who eat meat are base," using "meat-eating" to represent "wealthy and powerful families," which has the same meaning as "behind vermillion gates, wine and meat rot, while on the road, there are frozen corpses." Not only in China, but also in the West, this is even more prevalent. Looking at wartime frugality, specific "meatless days" are designated each week, and rationing is not as vigorous as rationing "one pound of beef" and "half a pound of butter." The whole world is truly a "meat world"!

Confucians say, "A gentleman keeps away from the kitchen." It is also said, "Hearing their cries, one cannot bear to eat their meat." Buddhists believe that abstaining from killing is a blessing for humanity. Currently, the spirit of killing pervades the globe, with mutual slaughter and devouring. The lives of the people are in great peril, and life is treated like child's play. There are no intact nests, and no peaceful lin in the depths. How much different are humans from cattle, sheep, chickens, and pigs? The ways of Huang Chao and Zhang Xianzhong are widely practiced.

Page 9

Recalling the Planning and Mobilization of the Past 160

— Weng Wenhao

The Double Tenth National Day is a day of great commemorative value in the minds of our national citizens. Let us imagine that before the founding of the Republic of China, China was under the control of thousands of years of imperial rule. All the officials of the imperial court were still there, and the army, specifically established to suppress the people, was well-trained and well-equipped. On the side advocating revolution, funds were extremely scarce, and weapons were lacking. Comparing the two sides, the material strength was vastly different. Undoubtedly, the revolutionary leaders were determined to save the country with fervent enthusiasm. They were unafraid of hardship and danger, persevering and undaunted, demonstrating a spirit of courageous advancement. They mobilized with great effort, without retreat, striving desperately to succeed. Finally, they succeeded in one fell swoop in Wuchang, creating the foundation for the Republic of China.

At that time, Shanghai bravely initiated reforms to boost morale, many provinces responded in unison, and the people of the whole country knew that the imperial system could not survive and the Republic of China must be established. It was only this belief of the majority of the people that was as firm as steel, causing the Qing Dynasty's civil and military officials to be fearful and apprehensive, possessing weapons but daring not use them, having power but failing to take effect, fleeing in droves, leading to complete failure.

It can be seen that the cause of the establishment of the Republic of China, in terms of material strength, was precisely using weakness to control strength, using poverty to defeat wealth. In terms of psychology, it was using righteousness to overcome wrong, using the new to replace the old. Moreover, comparing material strength with psychological belief, it was truly confidence that triumphed over material power. This is a fact of great value in history.

What was this indestructible confidence? At that time, the majority of the people accepted the leadership of the revolutionary leaders. Everyone deeply believed that the corruption and incompetence of the Qing Dynasty were the root cause of harming the country, and the imperial system, with its hereditary succession, was an outdated system. To save the country, it was necessary to innovate. Everyone recalled that after the Sino-Japanese War, foreign troubles were frequent, and China could not stand on its own without self-strengthening. They also recalled the Boxer Rebellion of the Gengzi year, which was reckless and destructive, and China could not become strong without innovation. Under this belief, once mobilized, everyone was of one mind, and this became the fundamental force for creating the Republic of China.

"Although Zhou was an old state, its mandate was new." Our country's new mandate entirely depended on this spirit of sincere upward progress. This confidence was also the main reason for our long-term resistance against Japan. At that time, after the Northeast fell in the September 18th Incident, Japanese aggression intensified, from the Northeast to North China, and then from North China to Central China, nibbling away like silkworms and devouring like whales, relentlessly advancing. Our country's territorial sovereignty was under grave threat. European and American allies were only seeking to protect themselves and made no promises to aid our country. Japan was strong and we were weak, the situation was obvious. However, our leader, the current President Chiang Kai-shek, resolutely decided to resist with military force, and the entire country supported him unanimously. A surge of activity arose, and everyone worked together, preparing for a long-term war to achieve final victory. Through years of effort, and after going through hardship, our lives were difficult but our spirit did not wane, and this ultimately caused European and American countries to admire and respect us, joining forces to wage war and force Japan to surrender. The land that our country had lost over the past fifty years, Taiwan and the Northeast, were all recovered and returned to our territory. This is a clear example proving that the people's confidence can ultimately achieve its goal. Where there's a will, there's a way; this is absolutely reliable.

What is deeply regrettable is that the country's path is full of difficulties. After winning the eight-year war of resistance, there was the disturbance of the Communist Party, which still caused smoke and dust to rise everywhere, and the people were unable to make a living. Last time, in order to clearly distinguish right from wrong and jointly face the national crisis, I already clearly stated that the Chinese Communist Party, since its establishment, has always been borrowing a name to destroy and devastate, becoming a fundamental disaster that shakes the country's economy and the people's livelihood. The necessity of our country's suppression of the rebellion is no less than the Xinhai Revolution and the war of resistance against Japan. In the past, the revolution and the war of resistance both achieved victory because of everyone's deep beliefs. The key to the success or failure of the current suppression of the rebellion also lies entirely in our fully strengthening our belief in certain victory.

The current practical difficulties are certainly particularly great, but comparing the current situation with the early stages of the revolution and the war of resistance, our government's organization, the army's equipment, the financial strength, and the convenience of transportation are all far above what they were in the past. We were able to win in the past, and we certainly cannot fail today. What I am concerned about is that the people's minds must thoroughly understand what is right and wrong and what is beneficial and harmful. They must not be swayed by the Communist Party's propaganda. They must unite sincerely and act consistently. They must not contradict each other, thereby reducing our own strength. They must be firm in their confidence and have no doubt. They must not ask the blind for directions and accept the other side's lies. On this Double Tenth National Day, I would like to encourage all compatriots across the country to not forget the loyalty, courage, and enthusiasm of the past, and to not neglect the important tasks of today's era.

Records of the Xinhai Revolution 161

— Published in this newspaper thirty-seven years ago — This newspaper's reference room

Revolutionaries in Wuhan Rise Up

[Hankou Telegram] Wuchang has fallen.

[Hankou Telegram] Before the festival, there were rumors in the E area that revolutionaries were rising up. It was initially scheduled for the 16th (October 7th), but it was unsuccessful due to strict prevention. It was then changed to the 18th (9th), but it was detected by a secret agent, and more than twenty revolutionaries were arrested, and dozens of boxes of explosives were seized. Knowing that the matter had failed, the party members agreed with the new army to rise up hastily on the 19th. The city had few soldiers, so it fell.

Yesterday, October 10th, revolutionaries in Wuchang rose up, and all government offices below the Governor-General were bombed. The telegraph office and various barracks were also destroyed. Governor-General Rui fled to a warship. Zhang Biao led his troops out of the government office but was killed by mutinying soldiers.

[Hankou Telegram] On the 18th (October 9th), the explosives hidden by revolutionaries in the Russian concession in Hankou suddenly fell to the ground and exploded. The detectives took away two revolutionaries, and the remaining party members secretly crossed the river on the 19th and besieged the Governor-General's office, throwing bombs fiercely. The Governor-General fled, and the office was destroyed.

[Hankou Telegram] The new army in the provincial capital of Hubei mutinied. The cavalry, infantry, sappers, and engineers that were transferred to defend the Governor-General's office turned against the government when they attacked the office, fought fiercely with the defending soldiers, and then drove the defending soldiers away. The office was also burned down.

[Hankou Telegram] It is said that four civil and military officials were killed during the riots. The family members of the Governor-General of Hubei fled to a certain warship and immediately set sail to Shanghai to take refuge.

[Hankou Telegram] It is said that Huang Xing led the revolutionaries in bombarding the government offices. All the party members were brave and forward, not retreating even in death.

[Hankou Telegram] The official troops outside Wuchang city and the revolutionaries have not ceased fighting. Commander Cen is safe. The Guangdong troops that were sent back to Guangdong have been ordered to stay in Shanghai temporarily pending reassignment. (The above telegrams were all published on October 12th)

[Hankou Telegram] Yingyang has also fallen. The prefect of Hanyang has fled without a trace.

[Hankou Telegram] This morning (October 12th), the revolutionary army besieged the Hanyang Arsenal and then occupied it, obtaining 20,000 rifles and many field guns and mountain guns. The soldiers guarding the arsenal expressed sympathy with the revolutionaries and did not resist. The Hanyang Ironworks, which is run by merchants, is safe and undisturbed.

[Hankou Telegram] The Governor-General of Hubei, Rui Cheng, is currently stationed in Hankou, telegraphing the Cabinet, saying, "I am willing to sacrifice myself and not restore the Qing Dynasty."

[Hankou Telegram] One association of the new army artillery, two teams of cavalry, a battalion of infantry engineers, and a battalion of construction engineers mutinied at the same time. At this time, only four battalions of infantry are available.

[Hankou Telegram] The Governor-General of Hubei is still stationed on the warship Chukan, and Hankou is still quiet.

[Hankou Telegram] Zhang Biao was injured but not killed. He has escaped to the warship where the Governor-General of Hubei is stationed.

[Hankou Telegram] Cen Xilin escaped danger in Hubei and will return to Shanghai in a few days.

[Hankou Telegram] According to the latest news, the Hanyang Ironworks has been seized by the revolutionaries, and the prefect of Hanyang and the Daotai of the Hanyang Customs have fled. The revolutionaries have now reached Hankou, but they treat foreigners with politeness. The Bank of China refuses to provide loans to foreigners. (Translated from the Zilin West Newspaper of the 12th)

[Hankou Telegram] On the afternoon of the 19th, a team of artillery, a team of infantry, and a battalion of engineers rose up in Wuchang and occupied the city. The Governor-General fled to a Chinese gunboat, and Zhang Biao fled to Hankou. They are currently attacking the Governor-General's office fiercely. It is said that a branch of the revolutionary army has gone to Hanyang. The overall situation is extremely critical. The people of various countries residing here have organized volunteer teams. The Japanese gunboat Sumida has gone to Wuhan. It is now feared that Hankou will also be affected. (Translated from the Wenhui Newspaper of the 11th)

[Hankou Telegram] Fighting is still ongoing in Wuchang, but at present, they are mostly engaged in searching for Manchus. The leader of the revolutionaries issued a proclamation, the main points of which are to expel the Manchus. The revolutionary government is responsible for protecting foreigners and the concessions of various countries, and those who violate this will be put to death. Yesterday, there was a rumor that Zhang Biao had died, but it is not yet confirmed. Chinese gunboats are now preparing for war. (Translated from the Wenhui Newspaper of the 20th) (The above telegrams were all published on October 13th)

[Hankou Telegram] The Hankou Mint and the Hanyang Steelworks have been occupied by the revolutionary army.

[Hankou Telegram] Last night, in the Chinese area of Hankou, bandits took the opportunity to set fires, which spread fiercely. The revolutionaries helped to extinguish the fires and then occupied the Chinese area, and immediately issued announcements to reassure the people, saying, "To prevent bandits from disturbing the safety of the people."

[Hankou Telegram] All the defense forces in Hankou have surrendered. Two battalions of the Bian army of the revolutionaries have arrived in Hubei. 12,000 men of the Beiyang Army are coming.

[Hankou Telegram] Wuchang, Hanyang, and Hankou have all been occupied by the revolutionaries, but they are responsible for protecting foreigners. The Hanyang Arsenal and gunpowder factory have also fallen into the hands of the revolutionaries. This afternoon, hundreds of revolutionary troops passed through the foreign concessions in Hankou to defend the train station. Fires are still breaking out in Wuchang. Hanyang and Hankou are now quiet. (Translated from the Wenhui Newspaper of October 12th)

[Hankou Telegram] The overall situation remains unchanged. Chinese gunboats that have not rebelled are patrolling the river, opening fire on the revolutionary army in Hanyang, as if the gunboats are also firing on Wuchang. According to Chinese sources, the Beijing-Hankou Railway has been destroyed by the revolutionaries 40 miles away from Hankou. (Translated from the Wenhui Newspaper of October 12th)

[Hankou Telegram] Yesterday, the revolutionaries occupied Wuchang, but many places in the city were burned. About two battalions of soldiers who have not rebelled are commanded by Zhang Biao. This morning, they left Wuchang and landed at the head of the Japanese concession. 500 soldiers from Shashi and Yichang have rushed back to Hankou on the Daji Maru, but these troops are the old subordinates of the revolutionary leader Li Yuanhong. (Translated from the Wenhui Newspaper of October 12th)

The official troops who have not rebelled are now waiting for the Bian army to arrive and will fight the revolutionaries in the middle of the Dazhi Gate and the riverbank station. The Japanese have organized a volunteer team and are working with people from various countries to protect the area. (The above telegrams were published on October 14th)

[Hankou Telegram] It is said that the revolutionary army has sunk a Chinese warship, and the remaining ships are cruising downstream.

Fearing that the Governor-General would be lost on the ship and that the concessions would be affected, they stopped firing again. (The above was published on October 15th)

The 6th and 4th Zhen, currently stationed in the north of Beijing, will be transported south by express train. Military movements are now being kept strictly secret to prevent the revolutionaries from destroying the railway. The railway south of Zhumadian has been managed by military officers, preventing ordinary cars from traveling, but the revolutionaries may bomb the Yellow River Bridge to prevent traffic. It is rumored that Sichuan is now in turmoil again, showing how widespread the revolutionaries have become. All the major officials in China are afraid that Guangzhou will rise up again. Beijing is under high alert. Special police officers have been selected today to protect the palace with guns. The grand parade on the 25th may be stopped. The Prince Regent has stopped summoning minor officials, apparently fearing that revolutionaries may have infiltrated. Core Work of Revolutionary Nation-Building 162

— He Yingqin

The work of revolutionary nation-building is of unparalleled difficulty and complexity. Thanks to the inspiring spirit of the Founding Father, the outstanding leadership of the President, and the courageous sacrifice of revolutionary martyrs and all the military and civilian compatriots, the revolutionary cause of the Three Principles of the People has been largely accomplished. Currently, the communist bandits are the last obstacle to the success of the revolution and the final stumbling block to the nation-building cause. We must all, with the ambition and spirit of revolutionaries, devote ourselves to the implementation of total war and the promotion of the frugal nation-building pact in our respective positions to sanction the treacherous and insidious communist bandits and ensure the victory of suppressing the rebellion and the success of nation-building. As long as the bandit scourge is eradicated, the country can enter a state of peace and prosperity, and our annual National Day commemoration will henceforth further promote its historical significance.

Anecdotes of the Double Tenth 163

— This newspaper's archives

Fifty Bullets Overthrew the Qing Dynasty

The Wuchang Uprising was launched in haste, and various preparations and communications were not sufficient in advance, but the result was a success, which shows the trend of popular sentiment. In the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, the Premier said in his training speech at the Whampoa Military Academy:

At that time, there were only about three hundred revolutionaries in Wuchang and Hankou, and only a few dozen real revolutionaries. All the guns had no bullets. They searched everywhere temporarily, and there were only two plates of bullets, a total of only fifty bullets. The revolutionaries were divided into fifty bullets, and they launched an attack in the engineering camp in the city, and the artillery battalion outside the city immediately responded. ... The revolutionaries only used dozens of people to fight more than 20,000 people, which can be said to be one person fighting five hundred people..."

According to the first attack, the engineering battalion in the city was the Eighth Battalion's left team led by Xiong Bingkun. At that time, the three martyrs Peng Chufan, Liu Yaozheng, and Yang Hongsheng were captured and killed by Ruizheng. The party members in the army were deeply afraid of exposure, and everyone was on guard, and the organization had been cracked and the roster had been checked. There was no way to wait until all preparations were completed before launching the attack, so they launched the attack in haste. Unexpectedly, as soon as the gunshots rang out, all the troops responded, and the Manchu officials immediately fled with their heads in their hands, and did not encounter any resistance, and the Republic of China was created from this.

The Story of the Qing Dynasty's Doomsday Prophecy

After the success of the Wuhan Uprising, Yuan Shikai was ordered by the Qing court to lead his troops south. Yuan was very superstitious. Before leaving, he asked a fortune teller to predict the fortune of this trip. The fortune teller said it would be very auspicious, so he left. The Hubei Military Government then wrote to Yuan, advising him not to work for the Qing Dynasty, and also explained the principles of divination, which was very interesting and also a talking point in the history of the founding of the Republic of China. The original book was quite fearful, and the following are a few excerpts:

"...I heard that you are going south under the orders of the Manchu court this time (referring to the southern expedition to supervise the army on September 11), you declined repeatedly, hesitated and considered three times, and even with the urging of Ruan Zhongshu and Yin Mao, you still did not decide immediately, and then you summoned a fortune teller to predict it. The fortune teller said that this trip would definitely establish a great cause, and then you started your journey. The words of the fortune teller have no value. You probably listened to it because of your gains and losses. Although you have the wonderful use of a hero, it is not as good as the ancients who used three obediences and two froms. If you really predict the direction of the hearts of 400 million people today, you should realize that the so-called great cause should be in the Republic of China, not in the dying Manchu court.

Do you really believe in astrology and prophecy? Then the folk songs and ancient prophecies circulating in our country were estimated by the people with foresight, and their predictions have been clearly confirmed today. Why don't you examine them? For example, "Holding a steel knife ninety-nine, only when everyone is killed will they stop." Do you know how to explain it? We also didn't understand it at first, but after the Manchu court's edict on the 21st of last month, the words "revolutionary party" suddenly appeared in it. Our clever people pointed it out, and we suddenly realized that there was a test. The word "revolutionary" has nine strokes, and the word "party" has nineteen strokes, which is the so-called "ninety-nine." Isn't it more obvious that the Hu Dynasty is coming to an end? Another example is "Continuing the rule in a remote area for thirty-six, the flags are divided into eight sides to Qin Prefecture," which is also a secret prophecy. Today, someone has also made a judgment on it. "Rule" refers to Emperor Xuantong, as everyone knows. "Remaining in a remote area for thirty-six" means that he can live in a remote area for thirty-six months, which is a clear sign that the Hu Dynasty will end in the third year of Xuantong. "Thirty-six" is a variant of three years. "Flags are divided into eight sides" means that the Eight Banners are scattered, and "Qin Prefecture" does not refer to Guanzhong. Now that Guanzhong is owned by the Republic of China, how can the chariot of the Gengzi Incident be stationed there again? "Qin" is an incomplete pictograph of the two characters "Fengtian," which means that the Manchu emperor will eventually be displaced in this Fengtian with incomplete sovereignty. In recent days, letters have come from Beijing saying that the Manchu Empress Dowager will flee to Fengtian. Isn't this a pre-determined sign? However, this secret record was not originally intended by us to advocate to fool the people. It is just that we heard that you recently believed in astrology and prophecy, so we chatted about it to get a smile, and also to clarify a proof of the end of history.

"However, the above is by no means the reason for our uprising this time. Because you are confused by omens and are afraid of gains and losses, we do not hesitate to break the rules and say a word for you, hoping that you will know that destiny belongs to you early, or you will not act recklessly on your own clever plans, be deceived for life, and fall into the evil crime of losing your body and the public. This is the intention of Guan and others to enlighten you..."

Historical Materials on the Founding of the Nation 165

— This newspaper's archives

(1) Articles of Association of the Revive China Society

The Revive China Society was founded in Honolulu in 1894, eighteen years before the founding of the Republic of China, and was the earliest Chinese revolutionary organization. At that time, ten articles of association were established, revealing its nature and purpose, the main points of which are as follows:

1. The name of the society should be correct. The name of this society is "Revive China Society," and the general assembly is located in China, and branch associations are located in various places.

2. The purpose should be clear. The purpose of the society is to connect Chinese people with lofty ideals at home and abroad, to study the science of wealth and strength, to revive China, and to maintain the national system. The reason why China's politics is becoming more and more non-existent, its principles are becoming more and more corrupt, and strong neighbors are despising the people is that everyone's hearts are not the same, and they only care about their current private interests, and do not care about the long-term overall situation. If China is divided by others, then our children and grandchildren will be slaves for generations, and their lives and property will not be guaranteed. There is nothing more urgent than this! But the whole country is indignant, but no one realizes it, no one saves it! Unite the wise and the foolish into one heart, unite the near and the far into one virtue, and pool our efforts to overcome great difficulties: then although China is in danger, it can be saved. The so-called people are the foundation of the country, and when the foundation is strong, the country is peaceful.

3. The ambition should be determined. The affairs to be determined by this society must be beneficial to the country and the people before they can be carried out: in order to assist the country above and achieve prosperity; and to protect the common people below and eliminate harshness. We must ensure that the 400 million people of China can each get what they want before we can be satisfied. If there are any who use this as an excuse to engage in fraud, form gangs for private gain, or divide boundaries and discriminate against each other, these are not the ambitions of this society: they should be resolutely eliminated in order to be fair and prevent abuses.

4. Personnel should be obtained. This society shall publicly hold personnel management once a year, and must select those with both good character and learning and those with comprehensive talent.

5. Friendship should be selective. This society shall only receive members who are recommended by two old members, and after the board of directors has judged that their hearts are bright, they are truly loyal and righteous, and they are sincerely concerned about their motherland and maintain China, so as to achieve a strong and prosperous place.

6. Branch associations should be widespread. People with lofty ideals from all directions can follow the articles of association and establish their own associations everywhere.

7. Talents should be gathered. This society is in urgent need of talents. Members are scattered in all directions, and they should always and everywhere seek out virtuous talents. Regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, if they are sincerely interested in benefiting the world and are willing to do their best for China, they can be admitted to the society.

8. Funds should be raised. The affairs managed by this society are of great importance, and a large amount of funds is required. Therefore, a silver association is specially established to raise funds to meet the urgent needs of the public and to provide a shortcut for shareholders to make money, which is a good deed that benefits both parties.

9. Public places should be established. Each branch association should establish a public place for members to work and for friends to talk from time to time, to discuss good methods for reviving China, to discuss current events, to study the politics of various countries, to express their own opinions, and to encourage each other to make progress. They must not engage in gambling games here, or do anything useless.

10. Flexibility should be good. Each clause is the outline for the opening of this society. Each branch association should make flexible changes according to local conditions and establish separate regulations to ensure that they are appropriate.

(2) Record of the Establishment of the Revolutionary Alliance

The Revolutionary Alliance was established in Tokyo, Japan, seven years before the founding of the Republic of China. According to Tian Tong's "The Establishment of the Revolutionary Alliance," an article in the first issue of the first volume of "Taiping Magazine," the establishment process is briefly described as follows:

In the summer of the year Yi Si, Sun Gong was about to come to Japan, and the comrades were excited. After arriving in Yokohama, Cheng Jiaquan conveyed the news again. Many students in Tokyo traveled between Tokyo and Yokohama. Sun Gong treated the virtuous with courtesy and also provided meals and lodging, personally holding a washbasin to wash the guests. The students in Tokyo held a welcome meeting at the Fujimiro, and many people attended. In the meeting, he gave a speech on the republican government. Wu Kun wrote it down, and the students were greatly moved, and the applause was thunderous. Then, a preparatory meeting of the Revolutionary Alliance was held at Cheng Jiaquan's residence in Iidamachi, with eight or nine people attending. They discussed various matters and the name of the society. Sun Gong advocated naming it the "Chinese Revolutionary Party," but Huang Gong said that this name would make it inconvenient for party members to act. After discussion, it was decided to name it the "Chinese Revolutionary Alliance." The oath format is as follows:

Oath taker, so-and-so from so-and-so province, so-and-so prefecture, so-and-so county, so-and-so, swears today to expel the Tartars, restore China, establish a republic, equalize land ownership, be faithful and loyal, and have a beginning and an end. If I violate this, I will be punished by the public. Member of the Chinese Revolutionary Alliance, so-and-so

Introducer, so-and-so

Heavenly Luck Year Month Day

The next day, a founding meeting was held at the residence of Uchida Ryohei in Hinokicho, Akasaka Ward, with more than 40 people attending. Everyone danced happily. Suddenly, Zhang Mingyi from Hunan said that the name was inappropriate and that the name should be established for the object since we have the ambition to overthrow the Manchu court. Sun said, it is not necessary, the Manchu government is corrupt, and we are therefore revolutionizing. Even if the Manchus sympathize with us, they can be allowed to join the party. Cao Yabo stood up and said, everyone advocates revolution today, and came here to start it. If there are any dissenting opinions, why come? Brothers, with a clear conscience, I will sign first, and everyone agreed, and each wrote an oath. The weather was hot that day, which was the 24th day of the sixth lunar month and the end of July of the new calendar. Uchida's servant brought cool cakes, and the comrades ate them heartily. In the laughter, the straw mat and wooden pillow were broken. The cups and plates were overturned, and some comrades fell to the ground. Sun Gong said, this is a sign of the overthrow of the Manchu government, and everyone rejoiced. Huang Xing, Jiang Zungui, Cheng Jiaquan, Ma Junwu and others were elected as drafters, and Sun Gong naturally participated in it. The main purpose of the regulations is to take the separation of powers, (1) the Executive Department, which is led by the Premier to manage affairs, and is divided into the General Affairs Department, the Secretariat Department, the Internal Affairs Department, the Foreign Affairs Department, the Accounting Department, and the Management Department. (2) The Deliberative Department, in which the councilors elect a speaker, and the speaker designates one councilor as the secretary. (3) The Judicial Department, with one chief, two judges, and one prosecutor. (4) Each provincial branch shall have one branch president. Several days later, a cadre election meeting was held at the residence of Viscount Banchamoto Kanemi in Reinan Saka. Huang Gong suggested that the comrades should consider that the position of Premier should belong to Sun Gong, which can save procedures and there is no need to vote. Everyone agreed, and Sun Gong was elected Premier, and Huang Gong was elected General Affairs. The remaining personnel of the Executive Department were gradually established, some were elected, and some were not elected. The councilors of the Deliberative Department were all elected at once, and the chiefs of the Judicial Department and the provincial branches were also elected later.

(3) Edict of Abdication of Emperor Xuantong

I, with reverence, have received the Edict of the Empress Dowager Longyu. Previously, due to the uprising of the people's army and the response from various provinces, the nine summers were boiling and the people were suffering. I specially ordered Yuan Shikai to send members to discuss the overall situation with the representatives of the Republic of China and to convene a parliament to make a public decision on the form of government. Since February, there has been no definite solution. The north and the south are separated and support each other. The negotiations have stopped on the way, and the soldiers are exposed in the wild. Only because the form of government is not decided for a day, the people's livelihood is not peaceful for a day. Now, the psychology of the people throughout the country is mostly inclined to the republic. The provinces in the south have advocated it in the past, and the generals in the north have also advocated it in the future. The direction of the people's hearts is known by Heaven. How can I bear to oppose the likes and dislikes of the people for the sake of the honor of one surname? Therefore, I observe the general situation externally and examine the feelings internally, and specially lead the emperor to return the ruling power to the whole country and set it as a republican constitutional government, to comfort the people in the country who are tired of chaos and hope for peace, and to learn from the ancient sages' meaning of the world for the public. Yuan Shikai was previously elected as Prime Minister by the Zizhengyuan. At this time of transition from the old to the new, there should be a way to unify the north and the south. Yuan Shikai should organize a provisional government and negotiate with the people's army on a unified plan, so that the people can live in peace and the country can be safe again. The five ethnic groups of Han, Manchu, Mongol, Hui, and Tibetan should still be completely integrated into a great Republic of China. I and the emperor can retreat to a wide and leisurely place, enjoy the years in peace, and receive the preferential treatment of the people for a long time, and witness the completion of Zhi Zhi. Isn't that beautiful? This is the order!

The date of the promulgation of the right edict was December 25, the third year of Xuantong, that is, February 5, the first year of the Republic of China.

(4) Zhang Puquan's Memoirs

Zhang Puquan's memoirs said: "On January 3, the third year of Xuantong, the Prime Minister went to Belgium. In May, I went to London. In the summer, I traveled to Switzerland with Wu Bigang, first living in Wengen, at the foot of the Jungfrau, and then moved to Grindelwald. In the autumn, the Wuchang Uprising broke out. The French were very excited to hear about the Chinese revolution. I took two or three friends and walked on the street. Four or five workers walked out of the hotel, took off their hats and shouted 'Long live China!' It can be seen that those who used to despise the Chinese have also changed their attitudes. I returned to China in November. When I arrived in Singapore, I heard that there were two factions in our party, one was the Revolutionary Alliance, and the other was the Restoration Society. I gathered people from both factions to drink together and explained the great righteousness. The main point is to avoid infighting among comrades on the day of the revolution's success. When I arrived in Shanghai, I heard that our army in Hankou had been defeated and the situation was very dangerous. Soon, the Prime Minister returned from overseas, and the morale was greatly boosted. I gave a lecture in a certain theater to raise funds for the revolutionary army. The women in the two boxes took off their gold and silver jewelry and threw them on the stage, which shows the excitement of the people's hearts. Ying Shi gathered wealthy merchants from Huzhou in a certain guild hall one day for the sake of raising funds, and closed the door, and they had to pay money. Ying Shi ordered me to give a speech."

(5) Provisional Grand President's Letter to Friendly Nations

Ever since the Manchus came to power, they have used supreme authority to impose unreasonable oppression, curtail civil rights, and resist public opinion. The intellectual, moral, and livelihood progress of our Republic of China has been delayed as a result. People of insight say that revolution is necessary to eliminate old filth and revitalize new opportunities. Fortunately, the banner of justice has been raised and the overall situation is about to be settled. We, the entire Republic of China, dare to announce to our friendly nations that we will overthrow the autocratic government of the Manchu Qing Dynasty and establish a republican republic.

Replacing the monarchy with a republic is not just a momentary anger of our people. Freedom is endowed by Heaven, and we have long yearned for it. We pray for lasting happiness and sweep away the obstacles in the future. We have cherished this small wish for a long time, but it has not been achieved. Today's events are the result of natural occurrence, and they are also the formal expression of the public opinion of our Republic.

Our Chinese nation is peaceful and law-abiding by nature. We will never lightly start a war unless we have no other choice but to defend ourselves. Therefore, since the Manchu Qing Dynasty stole China, for 168 years, the atrocities are too numerous to record. Our nation can only endure it and does not want to see the tragedy of bloodshed. We have risen up repeatedly, but it is difficult to achieve our goals. Today, we can no longer endure it, so we resort to force, hoping to free ourselves and our descendants from the shackles, and let freedom and happiness shine all over the world. It cannot be said that it is not a rare event in thousands of years.

The policy of the Manchu Qing government, to put it bluntly, is a tyrannical policy of jealousy of other races, selfishness, and unchangeable cruelty. We have suffered from it for a long time, and it is only natural that we have resorted to revolution. Destroying the old system and establishing a new country is something that we have to do. I would like to explain it to all the free nations of the world.

Before the Manchu Qing Dynasty stole the artifact, the civilized country of the Xia Dynasty allowed all countries in the world to communicate with each other and declare the freedom of religion. When the Ming Dynasty lost power, the Manchu barbarians came to power. Based on their narrow-mindedness and selfish prejudices, they set up various government orders to close themselves off and prevent the civilization of China from coming into contact with the countries of the world. As a result, the descendants of the gods are becoming more and more wild, and their natural abilities are difficult to develop. The people are imprisoned in ignorance. This is not only an obstacle to humanity, but also a public enemy of civilized countries.

Not only that, the Manchu Qing government wanted to keep the majority of the Han people permanently subservient to its autocracy, so that it could own wealth, cultivate and reproduce in it. Therefore, it did not hesitate to harm our people in order to benefit itself. The close relatives of the clan often had special privileges, and the majority of the civilians were subject to their control. It also levied exorbitant and illegal taxes and arbitrarily demanded them, which was close to robbery. It hindered the development of domestic business and hindered the prosperity of the colonial industry. The Manchu government did not know how to reward and protect the industry.

As for the use of people and administration, there is no principle of great justice. The harsh criminal system is inhuman. Selling official positions and granting titles, and politics is accomplished by bribery. The edicts are issued in the morning, and they are immediately violated in the evening, playing with our people, and it is not just once. Sitting and letting our country and our people be despised by the world, and they are almost unmoved by it.

We now want to eliminate the above-mentioned evils, so that our Republic of China can maintain friendly relations with all the countries in the world. Therefore, we do not hesitate to sacrifice our lives and fight against the evil government, and build a good one in its place. Therefore, I lay it out before the nations, and I hope that my friendly nations will take note of it. President of the Provisional Republic of China, I am related to Wen (signature).

The situation of the people's army's artillery positions in Hankou fiercely bombing the Qing army (Central News Agency)

Anecdotes of the Double Tenth 166

— This newspaper's archives

The Mystery of Li Yuanhong's Coming to Power

After Wuchang was occupied by the people's army, the revolutionaries negotiated in the Consultative Bureau to form a military and political department and elect a governor. However, due to the suddenness of the incident, party members with qualifications such as Liu Zhongwen, Liu Ying, Huang Keqiang, and Juju were not in Wuchang. The leaders of the various armies were too young to be summoned, and the situation was urgent, so it was not appropriate to be without a leader for a long time. Therefore, Li Yuanhong, the "good old man" of the 21st Mixed Brigade, who was not a member of the Revolutionary Party, was elected as the governor. Li's coming to power was not voluntary. According to Wen Gongzhi's "History of the Founding of the Republic of China" and Zou Lu's "Draft History of the Chinese Kuomintang," Li was dragged out from under the bed of Li's house by the party member Jiji Min. Zhang Nanxian's "Records of the Hubei Revolution" said that he was found by Ma Rong and Tang Qifa in the bedroom of Li's staff Liu Wenji. However, the Englishman Edwin J. Dingle said in his book "China's Revolution 1911-1912": "The Chinese Revolution is one of the most shocking epoch-making events in the history of the world. If Li Yuanhong, who is currently known to everyone in the world, was not there at that time, the revolution may not have broken out. History proves that only Li Yuanhong is the greatest reformer in China and the world? ..." I don't know if this gentleman is unaware of the facts or deliberately distorting them. Because regarding this matter, Li Yuanhong himself once sent a letter to Sa Zhenbing afterwards, which said:

"When the Wuchang Incident happened, the troops under Hong's command had already gone out to defend, and he was guarding the empty camp alone and was helpless. After the Party Army drove Supervisor Rui out of the city, they immediately led a team to Hong's camp, surrounded and searched. Hong changed into casual clothes and hid in the room, but was arrested. He was charged with righteousness. At that time, guns and cannons were lined up all around. If he didn't obey, he would be killed. Hong had to agree temporarily. My teacher knows that Hong is the most cautious and honest. How dare he do this rashly? ..."

From this, it can be seen that Li himself also admitted that he had "hidden in the room in casual clothes" at that time. As for saying that he was dragged out from under the bed, it may be an exaggeration by later generations, which is also unknown.

Historical Stories of the National Name and National Seal

After the Xinhai Restoration, the party members had different opinions on the official naming of the Republic of China. Some advocated setting it as "Great Han Country," and some advocated setting it as "Great Han Republic," all of which came from the change of the four characters "Great Qing Empire." Some people also advocated setting it as "Chinese Republic." When the Senate was established, the name "Republic of China" was determined.

The earliest person to propose the name "Republic of China" was Mr. Zhang Taiyan. Zhang once wrote an article in the "Min Bao" entitled "Explanation of the Republic of China," in which he extensively cited and explained the four characters in detail. The article said:

"The name of China is used to refer to the four Yi tribes. India also calls Magadha China, and Japan also calls Sanyang China. This is not unique to the Han land. If we talk about the Han land in terms of the Han land, then the name of China is bounded by the prefectures and counties of the pre-Han Dynasty. ... The name of the Chinese people is used to refer to the place where the ethnic group first arrived. The world says that Kunlun is the Chinese country, which is obtained by analogy with other things. Whether the former emperors of China ever established their capital in Kunlun, there is no clear evidence in history, and it is not enough to use it as evidence. However, the spirit of the gods comes from the West, and takes Yong and Liang prefectures as the foundation. Fuxi was born in Chengyi, Shennong was born in Jiangshui, and the Yellow Emperor lived in Qiaoshan. These are all the lands of Yong Prefecture. Gaoyang started in Ruoshui, Gaoxin started in Jiangshui, Shun lived in Xicheng, and Yu was born in Shiniu. These are all the lands of Liang Prefecture. By observing the birthplaces of the emperors, we can know that the core area of the ethnic group is the root. The land of Yong Prefecture extends southeast to Huaxian. The land of Liang Prefecture extends northeast to Huayang. By defining the boundary with Mount Hua, and naming the country Hua, the origin is like this..."

It can be seen that Mr. Taiyan named the two characters "China." "China" refers to the different countries outside the four borders, and "Hua" is because the ethnic group originated in Mount Hua, so it is used as the name of the founding of the country.

As for the national seal, the alliance used old jade, with the text "Seal of the Republic of China," two inches and seven minutes high, and two inches and six minutes wide. It was treated by the jade master Lu, and at that time, Yuan Shuaifu's secretary Lian Shenghai was specially appointed as the ink official to supervise the work. After the victory, the national government returned to the capital in triumph, and the one held by Wu Wenchang was this seal.
